no-nested-ternary	A			Stylistic Issues						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>Nesting ternary expressions can make code more difficult to understand.</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var foo = bar ? baz : qux === quxx ? bing : bam;\n</code></pre>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>The <code>no-nested-ternary</code> rule disallows nested ternary expressions.</p>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-nested-ternary: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nvar thing = foo ? bar : baz === qux ? quxx : foobar;\n\nfoo ? baz === qux ? quxx() : foobar() : bar();\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-nested-ternary: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nvar thing = foo ? bar : foobar;\n\nvar thing;\n\nif (foo) {\n  thing = bar;\n} else if (baz === qux) {\n  thing = quxx;\n} else {\n  thing = foobar;\n}\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-nested-ternary
no-new-object	A			Stylistic Issues						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>The <code>Object</code> constructor is used to create new generic objects in JavaScript, such as:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var myObject = new Object();\n</code></pre>\n<p>However, this is no different from using the more concise object literal syntax:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var myObject = {};\n</code></pre>\n<p>For this reason, many prefer to always use the object literal syntax and never use the <code>Object</code> constructor.</p>\n<p>While there are no performance differences between the two approaches, the byte savings and conciseness of the object literal form is what has made it the de facto way of creating new objects.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule disallows <code>Object</code> constructors.</p>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-new-object: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nvar myObject = new Object();\n\nvar myObject = new Object;\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-new-object: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nvar myObject = new CustomObject();\n\nvar myObject = {};\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-new-object
no-plusplus	A			Stylistic Issues						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>Because the unary <code>++</code> and <code>--</code> operators are subject to automatic semicolon insertion, differences in whitespace can change semantics of source code.</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var i = 10;\nvar j = 20;\n\ni ++\nj\n// i = 11, j = 20\n</code></pre>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var i = 10;\nvar j = 20;\n\ni\n++\nj\n// i = 10, j = 21\n</code></pre>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule disallows the unary operators <code>++</code> and <code>--</code>.</p>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-plusplus: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nvar foo = 0;\nfoo++;\n\nvar bar = 42;\nbar--;\n\nfor (i = 0; i &lt; l; i++) {\n    return;\n}\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-plusplus: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nvar foo = 0;\nfoo += 1;\n\nvar bar = 42;\nbar -= 1;\n\nfor (i = 0; i &lt; l; i += 1) {\n    return;\n}\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-plusplus
no-restricted-syntax	A			Stylistic Issues						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>JavaScript has a lot of language features, and not everyone likes all of them. As a result, some projects choose to disallow the use of certain language features altogether. For instance, you might decide to disallow the use of <code>try-catch</code> or <code>class</code>.</p>\n<p>Rather than creating separate rules for every language feature you want to turn off, this rule allows you to configure the syntax elements you want to restrict use of. These elements are represented by their <a href="https://github.com/estree/estree">ESTree</a> node types. For example, a function declaration is represented by <code>FunctionDeclaration</code> and the <code>with</code> statement is represented by <code>WithStatement</code>. You may find the full list of AST node names you can use <a href="https://github.com/eslint/espree/blob/master/lib/ast-node-types.js">on GitHub</a> and use the <a href="http://eslint.org/parser/">online parser</a> to see what type of nodes your code consists of.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule disallows specified (that is, user-defined) syntax.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-restricted-syntax
no-tabs	A			Stylistic Issues						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>Some style guides don't allow the use of tab characters at all, including within comments.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule looks for tabs anywhere inside a file: code, comments or anything else.</p>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var a /t= 2;\n\n/**\n* /t/t its a test function\n*/\nfunction test(){}\n\nvar x = 1; // /t test\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var a = 2;\n\n/**\n* its a test function\n*/\nfunction test(){}\n\nvar x = 1; // test\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-tabs
no-ternary	A			Stylistic Issues						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>The ternary operator is used to conditionally assign a value to a variable. no-trailing-spaces	A			Stylistic Issues\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>Sometimes in the course of editing files, you can end up with extra whitespace at the end of lines. These whitespace differences can be picked up by source control systems and flagged as diffs, causing frustration for developers. While this extra whitespace causes no functional issues, many code conventions require that trailing spaces be removed before check-in.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule disallows trailing whitespace (spaces, tabs, and other Unicode whitespace characters) at the end of lines.</p>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-trailing-spaces: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nvar foo = 0;//\nvar baz = 5;//\n//\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-trailing-spaces: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nvar foo = 0;\nvar baz = 5;\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-trailing-spaces
no-underscore-dangle	A			Stylistic Issues						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>As far as naming conventions for identifiers go, dangling underscores may be the most polarizing in JavaScript. Dangling underscores are underscores at either the beginning or end of an identifier, such as:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var _foo;\n</code></pre>\n<p>There is actually a long history of using dangling underscores to indicate &quot;private&quot; members of objects in JavaScript (though JavaScript doesn't have truly private members, this convention served as a warning). This began with SpiderMonkey adding nonstandard methods such as <code>__defineGetter__()</code>. The intent with the underscores was to make it obvious that this method was special in some way. Since that time, using a single underscore prefix has become popular as a way to indicate &quot;private&quot; members of objects.</p>\n<p>Whether or not you choose to allow dangling underscores in identifiers is purely a convention and has no effect on performance, readability, or complexity. It's purely a preference.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule disallows dangling underscores in identifiers.</p>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-underscore-dangle: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nvar foo_;\nvar __proto__ = {};\nfoo._bar();\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-underscore-dangle: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nvar _ = require('underscore');\nvar obj = _.contains(items, item);\nobj.__proto__ = {};\nvar file = __filename;\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-underscore-dangle
no-unneeded-ternary	A			Stylistic Issues\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>It's a common mistake in JavaScript to use a conditional expression to select between two Boolean values instead of using ! to convert the test to a Boolean.\nHere are some examples:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">// Bad\nvar isYes = answer === 1 ? true : false;\n\n// Good\nvar isYes = answer === 1;\n\n\n// Bad\nvar isNo = answer === 1 ? false : true;\n\n// Good\nvar isNo = answer !== 1;\n</code></pre>\n<p>Another common mistake is using a single variable as both the conditional test and the consequent. In such cases, the logical <code>OR</code> can be used to provide the same functionality.\nHere is an example:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">// Bad\nvar foo = bar ? bar : 1;\n\n// Good\nvar foo = bar || 1;\n</code></pre>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule disallow ternary operators when simpler alternatives exist.</p>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-unneeded-ternary: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nvar a = x === 2 ? true : false;\n\nvar a = x ? true : false;\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-unneeded-ternary: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nvar a = x === 2 ? &quot;Yes&quot; : &quot;No&quot;;\n\nvar a = x !== false;\n\nvar a = x ? &quot;Yes&quot; : &quot;No&quot;;\n\nvar a = x ? y : x;\n\nvar a = x ? x : 1;\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-unneeded-ternary
no-whitespace-before-property	A			Stylistic Issues\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>JavaScript allows whitespace between objects and their properties. However, inconsistent spacing can make code harder to read and can lead to errors.</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">foo. bar .baz . quz\n</code></pre>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule disallows whitespace around the dot or before the opening bracket before properties of objects if they are on the same line. This rule allows whitespace when the object and property are on separate lines, as it is common to add newlines to longer chains of properties:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">foo\n  .bar()\n  .baz()\n  .qux()\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-whitespace-before-property: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nfoo [bar]\n\nfoo. bar\n\nfoo .bar\n\nfoo. bar. baz\n\nfoo. bar()\n  .baz()\n\nfoo\n  .bar(). baz()\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-whitespace-before-property: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nfoo.bar\n\nfoo[bar]\n\nfoo[ bar ]\n\nfoo.bar.baz\n\nfoo\n  .bar().baz()\n\nfoo\n  .bar()\n  .baz()\n\nfoo.\n  bar().\n  baz()\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-whitespace-before-property
nonblock-statement-body-position	A			Stylistic Issues\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>When writing <code>if</code>, <code>else</code>, <code>while</code>, <code>do-while</code>, and <code>for</code> statements, the body can be a single statement instead of a block. It can be useful to enforce a consistent location for these single statements.</p>\n<p>For example, some developers avoid writing code like this:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">if (foo)\n  bar();\n</code></pre>\n<p>If another developer attempts to add <code>baz();</code> to the <code>if</code> statement, they might mistakenly change the code to</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">if (foo)\n  bar();\n  baz(); // this line is not in the `if` statement!\n</code></pre>\n<p>To avoid this issue, one might require all single-line <code>if</code> statements to appear directly after the conditional, without a linebreak:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">if (foo) bar();\n</code></pre>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule aims to enforce a consistent location for single-line statements.</p>\n<p>Note that this rule does not enforce the usage of single-line statements in general. If you would like to disallow single-line statements, use the <a href="/docs/rules/curly"><code>curly</code></a> rule instead.</p>\n<h3>Options</h3>\n<p>This rule accepts a string option:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><code>&quot;beside&quot;</code> (default) disallows a newline before a single-line statement.</li>\n<li><code>&quot;below&quot;</code> requires a newline before a single-line statement.</li>\n<li><code>&quot;any&quot;</code> does not enforce the position of a single-line statement.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Additionally, the rule accepts an optional object option with an <code>&quot;overrides&quot;</code> key. This can be used to specify a location for particular statements that override the default. For example:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><code>&quot;beside&quot;, { &quot;overrides&quot;: { &quot;while&quot;: &quot;below&quot; } }</code> requires all single-line statements to appear on the same line as their parent, unless the parent is a <code>while</code> statement, in which case the single-line statement must not be on the same line.</li>\n<li><code>&quot;below&quot;, { &quot;overrides&quot;: { &quot;do&quot;: &quot;any&quot; } }</code> disallows all single-line statements from appearing on the same line as their parent, unless the parent is a <code>do-while</code> statement, in which case the position of the single-line statement is not enforced.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule with the default <code>&quot;beside&quot;</code> option:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/* eslint nonblock-statement-body-position: [&quot;error&quot;, &quot;beside&quot;] */\n\nif (foo)\n  bar();\nelse\n  baz();\n\nwhile (foo)\n  bar();\n\nfor (let i = 1; i &lt; foo; i++)\n  bar();\n\ndo\n  bar();\nwhile (foo)\n\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule with the default <code>&quot;beside&quot;</code> option:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/* eslint nonblock-statement-body-position: [&quot;error&quot;, &quot;beside&quot;] */\n\nif (foo) bar();\nelse baz();\n\nwhile (foo) bar();\n\nfor (let i = 1; i &lt; foo; i++) bar();\n\ndo bar(); while (foo)\n\nif (foo) { // block statements are always allowed with this rule\n  bar();\n} else {\n  baz();\n}\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule with the <code>&quot;below&quot;</code> option:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/* eslint nonblock-statement-body-position: [&quot;error&quot;, &quot;below&quot;] */\n\nif (foo) bar();\nelse baz();\n\nwhile (foo) bar();\n\nfor (let i = 1; i &lt; foo; i++) bar();\n\ndo bar(); while (foo)\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule with the <code>&quot;below&quot;</code> option:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/* eslint nonblock-statement-body-position: [&quot;error&quot;, &quot;below&quot;] */\n\nif (foo)\n  bar();\nelse\n  baz();\n\nwhile (foo)\n  bar();\n\nfor (let i = 1; i &lt; foo; i++)\n  bar();\n\ndo\n  bar();\nwhile (foo)\n\nif (foo) {\n  // Although the second `if` statement is on the same line as the `else`, this is a very common\n  // pattern, so it's not checked by this rule.\n} else if (bar) {\n}\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule with the <code>&quot;beside&quot;, { &quot;overrides&quot;: { &quot;while&quot;: &quot;below&quot; } }</code> rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/* eslint nonblock-statement-body-position: [&quot;error&quot;, &quot;beside&quot;, { &quot;overrides&quot;: { &quot;while&quot;: &quot;below&quot; } }] */\n\nif (foo)\n  bar();\n\nwhile (foo) bar();\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule with the <code>&quot;beside&quot;, { &quot;overrides&quot;: { &quot;while&quot;: &quot;below&quot; } }</code> rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/* eslint nonblock-statement-body-position: [&quot;error&quot;, &quot;beside&quot;, { &quot;overrides&quot;: { &quot;while&quot;: &quot;below&quot; } }] */\n\nif (foo) bar();\n\nwhile (foo)\n  bar();\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/nonblock-statement-body-position
object-curly-newline	A			Stylistic Issues\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>A number of style guides require or disallow line breaks inside of object braces and other tokens.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule enforces consistent line breaks inside braces of object literals or destructuring assignments.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/object-curly-newline

object-property-newline	A			Stylistic Issues\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>While formatting preferences are very personal, a number of style guides require that object properties be placed on separate lines for better readability.</p>\n<p>Another argument in favor of this style is that it improves the readability of diffs when a property is changed:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-diff">// More readable\n var obj = {\n     foo: &quot;foo&quot;,\n-    bar: &quot;bar&quot;,\n+    bar: &quot;bazz&quot;,\n     baz: &quot;baz&quot;\n };\n</code></pre>\n<pre><code class="language-diff">// Less readable\n-var obj = { foo: &quot;foo&quot;, bar: &quot;bar&quot;, baz: &quot;baz&quot; };\n+var obj = { foo: &quot;foo&quot;, bar: &quot;bazz&quot;, baz: &quot;baz&quot; };\n</code></pre>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule aims to maintain consistency of newlines between object properties.</p>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint object-property-newline: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nvar obj = { foo: &quot;foo&quot;, bar: &quot;bar&quot;, baz: &quot;baz&quot; };\n\nvar obj2 = {\n    foo: &quot;foo&quot;, bar: &quot;bar&quot;, baz: &quot;baz&quot;\n};\n\nvar obj3 = {\n    foo: &quot;foo&quot;, bar: &quot;bar&quot;,\n    baz: &quot;baz&quot;\n};\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint object-property-newline: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nvar obj = {\n    foo: &quot;foo&quot;,\n    bar: &quot;bar&quot;,\n    baz: &quot;baz&quot;\n};\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/object-property-newline
one-var	A			Stylistic Issues						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>Variables can be declared at any point in JavaScript code using <code>var</code>, <code>let</code>, or <code>const</code>. There are many styles and preferences related to the declaration of variables, and one of those is deciding on how many variable declarations should be allowed in a single function.</p>\n<p>There are two schools of thought in this regard:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>There should be just one variable declaration for all variables in the function. That declaration typically appears at the top of the function.</li>\n<li>You should use one variable declaration for each variable you want to define.</li>\n</ol>\n<p>For instance:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">// one variable declaration per function\nfunction foo() {\n    var bar, baz;\n}\n\n// multiple variable declarations per function\nfunction foo() {\n    var bar;\n    var baz;\n}\n</code></pre>\n<p>The single-declaration school of thought is based in pre-ECMAScript 6 behaviors, where there was no such thing as block scope, only function scope. Since all <code>var</code> statements are hoisted to the top of the function anyway, some believe that declaring all variables in a single declaration at the top of the function removes confusion around scoping rules.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule enforces variables to be declared either together or separately per function ( for <code>var</code>) or block (for <code>let</code> and <code>const</code>) scope.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/one-var
one-var-declaration-per-line	A			Stylistic Issues\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>Some developers declare multiple var statements on the same line:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var foo, bar, baz;\n</code></pre>\n<p>Others prefer to declare one var per line.</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var foo,\n    bar,\n    baz;\n</code></pre>\n<p>Keeping to one of these styles across a project's codebase can help with maintaining code consistency.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule enforces a consistent newlines around variable declarations. operator-assignment	A			Stylistic Issues\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>JavaScript provides shorthand operators that combine variable assignment and some simple mathematical operations. For example, <code>x = x + 4</code> can be shortened to <code>x += 4</code>. The supported shorthand forms are as follows:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-text"> Shorthand | Separate\n-----------|------------\n x += y    | x = x + y\n x -= y    | x = x - y\n x *= y    | x = x * y\n x /= y    | x = x / y\n x %= y    | x = x % y\n x &lt;&lt;= y   | x = x &lt;&lt; y\n x &gt;&gt;= y   | x = x &gt;&gt; y\n x &gt;&gt;&gt;= y  | x = x &gt;&gt;&gt; y\n x &amp;= y    | x = x &amp; y\n x ^= y    | x = x ^ y\n x |= y    | x = x | y\n</code></pre>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule requires or disallows assignment operator shorthand where possible.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/operator-assignment

quote-props	A			Stylistic Issues\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>Object literal property names can be defined in two ways: using literals or using strings. For example, these two objects are equivalent:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var object1 = {\n    property: true\n};\n\nvar object2 = {\n    &quot;property&quot;: true\n};\n</code></pre>\n<p>In many cases, it doesn't matter if you choose to use an identifier instead of a string or vice-versa. Even so, you might decide to enforce a consistent style in your code.</p>\n<p>There are, however, some occasions when you must use quotes:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>If you are using an ECMAScript 3 JavaScript engine (such as IE8) and you want to use a keyword (such as <code>if</code>) as a property name. This restriction was removed in ECMAScript 5.</li>\n<li>You want to use a non-identifier character in your property name, such as having a property with a space like <code>&quot;one two&quot;</code>.</li>\n</ol>\n<p>Another example where quotes do matter is when using numeric literals as property keys:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var object = {\n    1e2: 1,\n    100: 2\n};\n</code></pre>\n<p>This may look alright at first sight, but this code in fact throws a syntax error in ECMAScript 5 strict mode. This happens because <code>1e2</code> and <code>100</code> are coerced into strings before getting used as the property name. Both <code>String(1e2)</code> and <code>String(100)</code> happen to be equal to <code>&quot;100&quot;</code>, which causes the &quot;Duplicate data property in object literal not allowed in strict mode&quot; error. Issues like that can be tricky to debug, so some prefer to require quotes around all property names.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule requires quotes around object literal property names.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/quote-props
quotes	A			Stylistic Issues\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>JavaScript allows you to define strings in one of three ways: double quotes, single quotes, and backticks (as of ECMAScript 6). require-jsdoc	A			Stylistic Issues						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p><a href="http://usejsdoc.org">JSDoc</a> is a JavaScript API documentation generator. For example, this is what a JSDoc comment looks like for a function:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/**\n * Adds two numbers together.\n * @param {int} num1 The first number.\n * @param {int} num2 The second number.\n * @returns {int} The sum of the two numbers.\n */\nfunction sum(num1, num2) {\n    return num1 + num2;\n}\n</code></pre>\n<p>Some style guides require JSDoc comments for all functions as a way of explaining function behavior.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule requires JSDoc comments for specified nodes. semi	A			Stylistic Issues\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>JavaScript is unique amongst the C-like languages in that it doesn't require semicolons at the end of each statement. In many cases, the JavaScript engine can determine that a semicolon should be in a certain spot and will automatically add it. This feature is known as <strong>automatic semicolon insertion (ASI)</strong> and is considered one of the more controversial features of JavaScript. For example, the following lines are both valid:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var name = &quot;ESLint&quot;\nvar website = &quot;eslint.org&quot;;\n</code></pre>\n<p>On the first line, the JavaScript engine will automatically insert a semicolon, so this is not considered a syntax error. The JavaScript engine still knows how to interpret the line and knows that the line end indicates the end of the statement.</p>\n<p>In the debate over ASI, there are generally two schools of thought. The first is that we should treat ASI as if it didn't exist and always include semicolons manually. The rationale is that it's easier to always include semicolons than to try to remember when they are or are not required, and thus decreases the possibility of introducing an error.</p>\n<p>However, the ASI mechanism can sometimes be tricky to people who are using semicolons. For example, consider this code:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">return\n{\n    name: &quot;ESLint&quot;\n};\n</code></pre>\n<p>This may look like a <code>return</code> statement that returns an object literal, however, the JavaScript engine will interpret this code as:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">return;\n{\n    name: &quot;ESLint&quot;;\n}\n</code></pre>\n<p>Effectively, a semicolon is inserted after the <code>return</code> statement, causing the code below it (a labeled literal inside a block) to be unreachable. This rule and the <a href="no-unreachable">no-unreachable</a> rule will protect your code from such cases.</p>\n<p>On the other side of the argument are those who says that since semicolons are inserted automatically, they are optional and do not need to be inserted manually. However, the ASI mechanism can also be tricky to people who don't use semicolons. For example, consider this code:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var globalCounter = { }\n\n(function () {\n    var n = 0\n    globalCounter.increment = function () {\n        return ++n\n    }\n})()\n</code></pre>\n<p>In this example, a semicolon will not be inserted after the first line, causing a run-time error (because an empty object is called as if it's a function). The <a href="no-unexpected-multiline">no-unexpected-multiline</a> rule can protect your code from such cases.</p>\n<p>Although ASI allows for more freedom over your coding style, it can also make your code behave in an unexpected way, whether you use semicolons or not. Therefore, it is best to know when ASI takes place and when it does not, and have ESLint protect your code from these potentially unexpected cases. In short, as once described by Isaac Schlueter, a <code>\n</code> character always ends a statement (just like a semicolon) unless one of the following is true:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>The statement has an unclosed paren, array literal, or object literal or ends in some other way that is not a valid way to end a statement. (For instance, ending with <code>.</code> or <code>,</code>.)</li>\n<li>The line is <code>--</code> or <code>++</code> (in which case it will decrement/increment the next token.)</li>\n<li>It is a <code>for()</code>, <code>while()</code>, <code>do</code>, <code>if()</code>, or <code>else</code>, and there is no <code>{</code></li>\n<li>The next line starts with <code>[</code>, <code>(</code>, <code>+</code>, <code>*</code>, <code>/</code>, <code>-</code>, <code>,</code>, <code>.</code>, or some other binary operator that can only be found between two tokens in a single expression.</li>\n</ol>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule enforces consistent use of semicolons.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/semi
semi-spacing	A			Stylistic Issues\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>JavaScript allows you to place unnecessary spaces before or after a semicolon.</p>\n<p>Disallowing or enforcing space around a semicolon can improve the readability of your program.</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var a = &quot;b&quot; ;\n\nvar c = &quot;d&quot;;var e = &quot;f&quot;;\n</code></pre>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule aims to enforce spacing around a semicolon. This rule prevents the use of spaces before a semicolon in expressions.</p>\n<p>This rule doesn't check spacing in the following cases:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>\n<p>The spacing after the semicolon if it is the first token in the line.</p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p>The spacing before the semicolon if it is after an opening parenthesis (<code>(</code> or <code>{</code>), or the spacing after the semicolon if it is before a closing parenthesis (<code>)</code> or <code>}</code>). That spacing is checked by <code>space-in-parens</code> or <code>block-spacing</code>.</p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p>The spacing around the semicolon in a for loop with an empty condition (<code>for(;;)</code>).</p>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/semi-spacing
sort-keys	A			Stylistic Issues						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>When declaring multiple properties, some developers prefer to sort property names alphabetically to be able to find necessary property easier at the later time. Others feel that it adds complexity and becomes burden to maintain.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule checks all property definitions of object expressions and verifies that all variables are sorted alphabetically.</p>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint sort-keys: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nlet obj = {a: 1, c: 3, b: 2};\nlet obj = {a: 1, &quot;c&quot;: 3, b: 2};\n\n// Case-sensitive by default.\nlet obj = {a: 1, b: 2, C: 3};\n\n// Non-natural order by default.\nlet obj = {1: a, 2: c, 10: b};\n\n// This rule checks computed properties which have a simple name as well.\n// Simple names are names which are expressed by an Identifier node or a Literal node.\nconst S = Symbol(&quot;s&quot;)\nlet obj = {a: 1, [&quot;c&quot;]: 3, b: 2};\nlet obj = {a: 1, [S]: 3, b: 2};\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint sort-keys: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nlet obj = {a: 1, b: 2, c: 3};\nlet obj = {a: 1, &quot;b&quot;: 2, c: 3};\n\n// Case-sensitive by default.\nlet obj = {C: 3, a: 1, b: 2};\n\n// Non-natural order by default.\nlet obj = {1: a, 10: b, 2: c};\n\n// This rule checks computed properties which have a simple name as well.\nlet obj = {a: 1, [&quot;b&quot;]: 2, c: 3};\nlet obj = {a: 1, [b]: 2, c: 3};\n\n// This rule ignores computed properties which have a non-simple name.\nlet obj = {a: 1, [c + d]: 3, b: 2};\nlet obj = {a: 1, [&quot;c&quot; + &quot;d&quot;]: 3, b: 2};\nlet obj = {a: 1, [`${c}`]: 3, b: 2};\nlet obj = {a: 1, [tag`c`]: 3, b: 2};\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/sort-keys
sort-vars	A			Stylistic Issues						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>When declaring multiple variables within the same block, some developers prefer to sort variable names alphabetically to be able to find necessary variable easier at the later time. Others feel that it adds complexity and becomes burden to maintain.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule checks all variable declaration blocks and verifies that all variables are sorted alphabetically.\nThe default configuration of the rule is case-sensitive.</p>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint sort-vars: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nvar b, a;\n\nvar a, B, c;\n\nvar a, A;\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint sort-vars: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nvar a, b, c, d;\n\nvar _a = 10;\nvar _b = 20;\n\nvar A, a;\n\nvar B, a, c;\n</code></pre>\n<p>Alphabetical list is maintained starting from the first variable and excluding any that are considered problems. So the following code will produce two problems:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint sort-vars: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nvar c, d, a, b;\n</code></pre>\n<p>But this one, will only produce one:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint sort-vars: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nvar c, d, a, e;\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/sort-vars
space-before-blocks	A			Stylistic Issues\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>Consistency is an important part of any style guide.\nWhile it is a personal preference where to put the opening brace of blocks,\nit should be consistent across a whole project.\nHaving an inconsistent style distracts the reader from seeing the important parts of the code.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule will enforce consistency of spacing before blocks. It is only applied on blocks that dont begin on a new line.</p>\n<ul>\n<li>This rule ignores spacing which is between <code>=&gt;</code> and a block. The spacing is handled by the <code>arrow-spacing</code> rule.</li>\n<li>This rule ignores spacing which is between a keyword and a block. The spacing is handled by the <code>keyword-spacing</code> rule.</li>\n</ul>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/space-before-blocks
space-before-function-paren	A			Stylistic Issues\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>When formatting a function, whitespace is allowed between the function name or <code>function</code> keyword and the opening paren. Named functions also require a space between the <code>function</code> keyword and the function name, but anonymous functions require no whitespace. For example:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">function withoutSpace(x) {\n    // ...\n}\n\nfunction withSpace (x) {\n    // ...\n}\n\nvar anonymousWithoutSpace = function() {};\n\nvar anonymousWithSpace = function () {};\n</code></pre>\n<p>Style guides may require a space after the <code>function</code> keyword for anonymous functions, while others specify no whitespace. Similarly, the space after a function name may or may not be required.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule aims to enforce consistent spacing before function parentheses and as such, will warn whenever whitespace doesn't match the preferences specified.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/space-before-function-paren
space-in-parens	A			Stylistic Issues\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>Some style guides require or disallow spaces inside of parentheses:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">foo( 'bar' );\nvar x = ( 1 + 2 ) * 3;\n\nfoo('bar');\nvar x = (1 + 2) * 3;\n</code></pre>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule will enforce consistency of spacing directly inside of parentheses, by disallowing or requiring one or more spaces to the right of <code>(</code> and to the left of <code>)</code>. In either case, <code>()</code> will still be allowed.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/space-in-parens
space-infix-ops	A			Stylistic Issues\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>While formatting preferences are very personal, a number of style guides require spaces around operators, such as:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var sum = 1 + 2;\n</code></pre>\n<p>The proponents of these extra spaces believe it make the code easier to read and can more easily highlight potential errors, such as:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var sum = i+++2;\n</code></pre>\n<p>While this is valid JavaScript syntax, it is hard to determine what the author intended.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule is aimed at ensuring there are spaces around infix operators.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/space-infix-ops
space-unary-ops	A			Stylistic Issues\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>Some style guides require or disallow spaces before or after unary operators. template-tag-spacing	A			Stylistic Issues\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>With ES6, it's possible to create functions called <a href="#further-reading">tagged template literals</a> where the function parameters consist of a template literal's strings and expressions.</p>\n<p>When using tagged template literals, it's possible to insert whitespace between the tag function and the template literal. unicode-bom	A			Stylistic Issues\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>The Unicode Byte Order Mark (BOM) is used to specify whether code units are big\nendian or little endian. That is, whether the most significant or least\nsignificant bytes come first. UTF-8 does not require a BOM because byte ordering\ndoes not matter when characters are a single byte. Since UTF-8 is the dominant\nencoding of the web, we make <code>&quot;never&quot;</code> the default option.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>If the <code>&quot;always&quot;</code> option is used, this rule requires that files always begin\nwith the Unicode BOM character U+FEFF. wrap-regex	A			Stylistic Issues\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>When a regular expression is used in certain situations, it can end up looking like a division operator. arrow-parens	A			ECMAScript 6\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>Arrow functions can omit parentheses when they have exactly one parameter. arrow-spacing	A			ECMAScript 6\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>This rule normalize style of spacing before/after an arrow function's arrow(<code>=&gt;</code>).</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint-env es6*/\n\n// { &quot;before&quot;: true, &quot;after&quot;: true }\n(a) =&gt; {};\n(a) =&gt; {};\na =&gt; a;\n() =&gt; {'\n'};\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule with the <code>{ &quot;before&quot;: false, &quot;after&quot;: false }</code> option:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint arrow-spacing: [&quot;error&quot;, { &quot;before&quot;: false, &quot;after&quot;: false }]*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\n() =&gt;{};\n(a) =&gt; {};\n()=&gt; {'\n'};\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule with the <code>{ &quot;before&quot;: false, &quot;after&quot;: false }</code> option:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint arrow-spacing: [&quot;error&quot;, { &quot;before&quot;: false, &quot;after&quot;: false }]*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\n()=&gt;{};\n(a)=&gt;{};\n()=&gt;{'\n'};\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule with the <code>{ &quot;before&quot;: false, &quot;after&quot;: true }</code> option:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint arrow-spacing: [&quot;error&quot;, { &quot;before&quot;: false, &quot;after&quot;: true }]*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\n() =&gt;{};\n(a) =&gt; constructor-super	A			ECMAScript 6\nRecommended Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(recommended) The <code>&quot;extends&quot;: &quot;eslint:recommended&quot;</code> property in a configuration file enables this rule.</p>\n<p>Constructors of derived classes must call <code>super()</code>.\nConstructors of non derived classes must not call <code>super()</code>.\nIf this is not observed, the javascript engine will raise a runtime error.</p>\n<p>This rule checks whether or not there is a valid <code>super()</code> call.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule is aimed to flag invalid/missing <code>super()</code> calls.</p>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint constructor-super: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nclass A {\n    constructor() {\n        super();  // This is a SyntaxError.\n    }\n}\n\nclass A extends B {\n    constructor() { }  // Would throw a ReferenceError.\n}\n\n// Classes which inherits from a non constructor are always problems.\nclass A extends null {\n    constructor() {\n        super();  // Would throw a TypeError.\n    }\n}\n\nclass A extends null {\n    constructor() { }  // Would throw a ReferenceError.\n}\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint constructor-super: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nclass A {\n    constructor() { }\n}\n\nclass A extends B {\n    constructor() {\n        super();\n    }\n}\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/constructor-super
generator-star-spacing	A			ECMAScript 6\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>Generators are a new type of function in ECMAScript 6 that can return multiple values over time.\nThese special functions are indicated by placing an <code>*</code> after the <code>function</code> keyword.</p>\n<p>Here is an example of a generator function:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nfunction* generator() {\n    yield &quot;44&quot;;\n    yield &quot;55&quot;;\n}\n</code></pre>\n<p>This is also valid:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nfunction *generator() {\n    yield &quot;44&quot;;\n    yield &quot;55&quot;;\n}\n</code></pre>\n<p>This is valid as well:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nfunction * generator() {\n    yield &quot;44&quot;;\n    yield &quot;55&quot;;\n}\n</code></pre>\n<p>To keep a sense of consistency when using generators this rule enforces a single position for the <code>*</code>.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule aims to enforce spacing around the <code>*</code> of generator functions.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/generator-star-spacing
no-class-assign	A			ECMAScript 6\nRecommended Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(recommended) The <code>&quot;extends&quot;: &quot;eslint:recommended&quot;</code> property in a configuration file enables this rule.</p>\n<p><code>ClassDeclaration</code> creates a variable, and we can modify the variable.</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nclass A { }\nA = 0;\n</code></pre>\n<p>But the modification is a mistake in most cases.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule is aimed to flag modifying variables of class declarations.</p>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-class-assign: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nclass A { }\nA = 0;\n</code></pre>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-class-assign: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nA = 0;\nclass A { }\n</code></pre>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-class-assign: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nclass A {\n    b() {\n        A = 0;\n    }\n}\n</code></pre>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-class-assign: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nlet A = class A {\n    b() {\n        A = 0;\n        // `let A` is shadowed by the class name.\n    }\n}\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-class-assign: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nlet A = class A { }\nA = 0; // A is a variable.\n</code></pre>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-class-assign: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nlet A = class {\n    b() {\n        A = 0; // A is a variable.\n    }\n}\n</code></pre>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-class-assign: 2*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nclass A {\n    b(A) {\n        A = 0; // A is a parameter.\n    }\n}\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-class-assign
no-confusing-arrow	A			ECMAScript 6						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>Arrow functions (<code>=&gt;</code>) are similar in syntax to some comparison operators (<code>&gt;</code>, <code>&lt;</code>, <code>&lt;=</code>, and <code>&gt;=</code>). This rule warns against using the arrow function syntax in places where it could be confused with a comparison operator. Even if the arguments of the arrow function are wrapped with parens, this rule still warns about it unless <code>allowParens</code> is set to <code>true</code>.</p>\n<p>Here's an example where the usage of <code>=&gt;</code> could be confusing:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">// The intent is not clear\nvar x = a =&gt; 1 ? 2 : 3;\n// Did the author mean this\nvar x = function (a) { return 1 ? 2 : 3 };\n// Or this\nvar x = a &lt;= 1 ? 2 : 3;\n</code></pre>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-confusing-arrow: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nvar x = a =&gt; 1 ? 2 : 3;\nvar x = (a) =&gt; 1 ? 2 : 3;\nvar x = (a) =&gt; (1 ? 2 : 3);\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-confusing-arrow: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nvar x = a =&gt; { return 1 ? 2 : 3; };\nvar x = (a) =&gt; { return 1 ? 2 : 3; };\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-confusing-arrow
no-const-assign	A			ECMAScript 6\nRecommended Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(recommended) The <code>&quot;extends&quot;: &quot;eslint:recommended&quot;</code> property in a configuration file enables this rule.</p>\n<p>We cannot modify variables that are declared using <code>const</code> keyword.\nIt will raise a runtime error.</p>\n<p>Under non ES2015 environment, it might be ignored merely.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule is aimed to flag modifying variables that are declared using <code>const</code> keyword.</p>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-const-assign: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nconst a = 0;\na = 1;\n</code></pre>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-const-assign: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nconst a = 0;\na += 1;\n</code></pre>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-const-assign: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nconst a = 0;\n++a;\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-const-assign: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nconst a = 0;\nconsole.log(a);\n</code></pre>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-const-assign: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nfor (const a in [1, 2, 3]) { // `a` is re-defined (not modified) on each loop step.\n    console.log(a);\n}\n</code></pre>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-const-assign: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nfor (const a of [1, 2, 3]) { // `a` is re-defined (not modified) on each loop step.\n    console.log(a);\n}\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-const-assign
no-dupe-class-members	A			ECMAScript 6\nRecommended Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(recommended) The <code>&quot;extends&quot;: &quot;eslint:recommended&quot;</code> property in a configuration file enables this rule.</p>\n<p>If there are declarations of the same name in class members, the last declaration overwrites other declarations silently.\nIt can cause unexpected behaviors.</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nclass Foo {\n  bar() { console.log(&quot;hello&quot;); }\n  bar() { console.log(&quot;goodbye&quot;); }\n}\n\nvar foo = new Foo();\nfoo.bar(); // goodbye\n</code></pre>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule is aimed to flag the use of duplicate names in class members.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-dupe-class-members
no-duplicate-imports	A			ECMAScript 6						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>Using a single <code>import</code> statement per module will make the code clearer because you can see everything being imported from that module on one line.</p>\n<p>In the following example the <code>module</code> import on line 1 is repeated on line 3. These can be combined to make the list of imports more succinct.</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">import { merge } from 'module';\nimport something from 'another-module';\nimport { find } from 'module';\n</code></pre>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rules requires that all imports from a single module exists in a single <code>import</code> statement.</p>\n<p>Example of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-duplicate-imports: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nimport { merge } from 'module';\nimport something from 'another-module';\nimport { find } from 'module';\n</code></pre>\n<p>Example of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint no-duplicate-imports: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nimport { merge, find } from 'module';\nimport something from 'another-module';\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-duplicate-imports
no-new-symbol	A			ECMAScript 6\nRecommended Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(recommended) The <code>&quot;extends&quot;: &quot;eslint:recommended&quot;</code> property in a configuration file enables this rule.</p>\n<p><code>Symbol</code> is not intended to be used with the <code>new</code> operator, but to be called as a function.</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var foo = new Symbol(&quot;foo&quot;);\n</code></pre>\n<p>This throws a <code>TypeError</code> exception.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule is aimed at preventing the accidental calling of <code>Symbol</code> with the <code>new</code> operator.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-new-symbol
no-restricted-imports	A			ECMAScript 6						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>Imports are an ES6/ES2015 standard for making the functionality of other modules available in your current module. In CommonJS this is implemented through the require() call which makes this ESLint rule roughly equivalent to its CommonJS counterpart <code>no-restricted-modules</code>.</p>\n<p>Why would you want to restrict imports?</p>\n<ul>\n<li>\n<p>Some imports might not make sense in a particular environment. For example, Node.js' <code>fs</code> module would not make sense in an environment that didn't have a file system.</p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p>Some modules provide similar or identical functionality, think <code>lodash</code> and <code>underscore</code>. Your project may have standardized on a module. You want to make sure that the other alternatives are not being used as this would unnecessarily bloat the project and provide a higher maintenance cost of two dependencies when one would suffice.</p>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule allows you to specify imports that you don't want to use in your application.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-restricted-imports
no-this-before-super	A			ECMAScript 6\nRecommended Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(recommended) The <code>&quot;extends&quot;: &quot;eslint:recommended&quot;</code> property in a configuration file enables this rule.</p>\n<p>In the constructor of derived classes, if <code>this</code>/<code>super</code> are used before <code>super()</code> calls, it raises a reference error.</p>\n<p>This rule checks <code>this</code>/<code>super</code> keywords in constructors, then reports those that are before <code>super()</code>.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule is aimed to flag <code>this</code>/<code>super</code> keywords before <code>super()</code> callings.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-this-before-super
no-useless-computed-key	A			ECMAScript 6\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>It's unnecessary to use computed properties with literals such as:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var foo = {[&quot;a&quot;]: &quot;b&quot;};\n</code></pre>\n<p>The code can be rewritten as:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var foo = {&quot;a&quot;: &quot;b&quot;};\n</code></pre>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule disallows unnecessary usage of computed property keys.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-useless-computed-key
no-useless-constructor	A			ECMAScript 6						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>ES2015 provides a default class constructor if one is not specified. As such, it is unnecessary to provide an empty constructor or one that simply delegates into its parent class, as in the following examples:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">class A {\n    constructor () {\n    }\n}\n\nclass A extends B {\n    constructor (value) {\n      super(value);\n    }\n}\n</code></pre>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule flags class constructors that can be safely removed without changing how the class works.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-useless-constructor
no-useless-rename	A			ECMAScript 6\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>ES2015 allows for the renaming of references in import and export statements as well as destructuring assignments. This gives programmers a concise syntax for performing these operations while renaming these references:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">import { foo as bar } from &quot;baz&quot;;\nexport { foo as bar };\nlet { foo: bar } = baz;\n</code></pre>\n<p>With this syntax, it is possible to rename a reference to the same name. This is a completely redundant operation, as this is the same as not renaming at all. For example, this:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">import { foo as foo } from &quot;bar&quot;;\nexport { foo as foo };\nlet { foo: foo } = bar;\n</code></pre>\n<p>is the same as:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">import { foo } from &quot;bar&quot;;\nexport { foo };\nlet { foo } = bar;\n</code></pre>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule disallows the renaming of import, export, and destructured assignments to the same name.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-useless-rename
no-var	A			ECMAScript 6\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>ECMAScript 6 allows programmers to create variables with block scope instead of function scope using the <code>let</code>\nand <code>const</code> keywords. Block scope is common in many other programming languages and helps programmers avoid mistakes\nsuch as:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var count = people.length;\nvar enoughFood = count &gt; sandwiches.length;\n\nif (enoughFood) {\n    var count = sandwiches.length; // accidently overriding the count variable\n    console.log(&quot;We have &quot; + count + &quot; sandwiches for everyone. Plenty for all!&quot;);\n}\n\n// our count variable is no longer accurate\nconsole.log(&quot;We have &quot; + count + &quot; people and &quot; + sandwiches.length + &quot; sandwiches!&quot;);\n</code></pre>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule is aimed at discouraging the use of <code>var</code> and encouraging the use of <code>const</code> or <code>let</code> instead.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-var
object-shorthand	A			ECMAScript 6\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>EcmaScript 6 provides a concise form for defining object literal methods and properties. This\nsyntax can make defining complex object literals much cleaner.</p>\n<p>Here are a few common examples using the ES5 syntax:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">// properties\nvar foo = {\n    x: x,\n    y: y,\n    z: z,\n};\n\n// methods\nvar foo = {\n    a: function() {},\n    b: function() {}\n};\n</code></pre>\n<p>Now here are ES6 equivalents:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint-env es6*/\n\n// properties\nvar foo = {x, y, z};\n\n// methods\nvar foo = {\n    a() {},\n    b() {}\n};\n</code></pre>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule enforces the use of the shorthand syntax. This applies\nto all methods (including generators) defined in object literals and any\nproperties defined where the key name matches name of the assigned variable.</p>\n<p>Each of the following properties would warn:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint object-shorthand: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nvar foo = {\n    w: function() {},\n    x: function *() {},\n    [y]: function() {},\n    z: z\n};\n</code></pre>\n<p>In that case the expected syntax would have been:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint object-shorthand: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nvar foo = {\n    w() {},\n    *x() {},\n    [y]() {},\n    z\n};\n</code></pre>\n<p>This rule does not flag arrow functions inside of object literals.\nThe following will <em>not</em> warn:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint object-shorthand: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nvar foo = {\n    x: (y) =&gt; y\n};\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/object-shorthand
prefer-arrow-callback	A			ECMAScript 6\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>Arrow functions are suited to callbacks, because:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><code>this</code> keywords in arrow functions bind to the upper scope's.</li>\n<li>The notation of the arrow function is shorter than function expression's.</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule is aimed to flag usage of function expressions in an argument list.</p>\n<p>The following patterns are considered problems:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint prefer-arrow-callback: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nfoo(function(a) { return a; });\nfoo(function() { return this.a; }.bind(this));\n</code></pre>\n<p>The following patterns are not considered problems:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint prefer-arrow-callback: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nfoo(a =&gt; a);\nfoo(function*() { yield; });\n\n// this is not a callback.\nvar foo = function foo(a) { return a; };\n\n// using `this` without `.bind(this)`.\nfoo(function() { return this.a; });\n\n// recursively.\nfoo(function bar(n) { return n &amp;&amp; n + bar(n - 1); });\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/prefer-arrow-callback
prefer-const	A			ECMAScript 6\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>If a variable is never reassigned, using the <code>const</code> declaration is better.</p>\n<p><code>const</code> declaration tells readers, &quot;this variable is never reassigned,&quot; reducing cognitive load and improving maintainability.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule is aimed at flagging variables that are declared using <code>let</code> keyword, but never reassigned after the initial assignment.</p>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint prefer-const: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\n// it's initialized and never reassigned.\nlet a = 3;\nconsole.log(a);\n\nlet a;\na = 0;\nconsole.log(a);\n\n// `i` is redefined (not reassigned) on each loop step.\nfor (let i in [1, 2, 3]) {\n    console.log(i);\n}\n\n// `a` is redefined (not reassigned) on each loop step.\nfor (let a of [1, 2, 3]) {\n    console.log(a);\n}\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint prefer-const: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\n// using const.\nconst a = 0;\n\n// it's never initialized.\nlet a;\nconsole.log(a);\n\n// it's reassigned after initialized.\nlet a;\na = 0;\na = 1;\nconsole.log(a);\n\n// it's initialized in a different block from the declaration.\nlet a;\nif (true) {\n    a = 0;\n}\nconsole.log(a);\n\n// it's initialized at a place that we cannot write a variable declaration.\nlet a;\nif (true) a = 0;\nconsole.log(a);\n\n// `i` gets a new binding each iteration\nfor (const i in [1, 2, 3]) {\n  console.log(i);\n}\n\n// `a` gets a new binding each iteration\nfor (const a of [1, 2, 3]) {\n  console.log(a);\n}\n\n// `end` is never reassigned, but we cannot separate the declarations without modifying the scope.\nfor (let i = 0, end = 10; i &lt; end; ++i) {\n    console.log(a);\n}\n\n// suggest to use `no-var` rule.\nvar b = 3;\nconsole.log(b);\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/prefer-const
prefer-destructuring	A			ECMAScript 6						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>With JavaScript ES6, a new syntax was added for creating variables from an array index or object property, called <a href="#further-reading">destructuring</a>.  This rule enforces usage of destructuring instead of accessing a property through a member expression.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-javascript">// With `array` enabled\nvar foo = array[0];\n\n// With `object` enabled\nvar foo = object.foo;\nvar foo = object['foo'];\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-javascript">// With `array` enabled\nvar [ foo ] = array;\nvar foo = array[someIndex];\n\n// With `object` enabled\nvar { foo } = object;\nvar foo = object.bar;\n</code></pre>\n<h3>Options</h3>\n<p>This rule takes two sets of configuration objects; the first controls the types that the rule is applied to, and the second controls the way those objects are evaluated.</p>\n<p>The first has two properties, <code>array</code> and <code>object</code>, which can be used to turn on or off the destructuring requirement for each of those types independently.  By default, both are <code>true</code>.</p>\n<p>The second has a single property, <code>enforceForRenamedProperties</code>, that controls whether or not the <code>object</code> destructuring rules are applied in cases where the variable requires the property being access to be renamed.</p>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code when <code>enforceForRenamedProperties</code> is enabled:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-javascript">var foo = object.bar;\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code when <code>enforceForRenamedProperties</code> is enabled:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-javascript">var { bar: foo } = object;\n</code></pre>\n<p>An example configuration, with the defaults filled in, looks like this:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-json">{\n  &quot;rules&quot;: {\n    &quot;prefer-destructuring&quot;: [&quot;error&quot;, {\n      &quot;array&quot;: true,\n      &quot;object&quot;: true\n    }, {\n      &quot;enforceForRenamedProperties&quot;: false\n    }]\n  }\n}\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/prefer-destructuring
prefer-numeric-literals	A			ECMAScript 6\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>The <code>parseInt()</code> function can be used to turn binary, octal, and hexadecimal strings into integers. As binary, octal, and hexadecimal literals are supported in ES6, this rule encourages use of those numeric literals instead of <code>parseInt()</code>.</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">0b111110111 === 503;\n0o767 === 503;\n</code></pre>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule disallows <code>parseInt()</code> if it is called with two arguments: a string and a radix option of 2 (binary), 8 (octal), or 16 (hexadecimal).</p>\n<p>Examples of <strong>incorrect</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint prefer-numeric-literals: &quot;error&quot;*/\n\nparseInt(&quot;111110111&quot;, 2) === 503;\nparseInt(&quot;767&quot;, 8) === 503;\nparseInt(&quot;1F7&quot;, 16) === 255;\n</code></pre>\n<p>Examples of <strong>correct</strong> code for this rule:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint prefer-numeric-literals: &quot;error&quot;*/\n/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nparseInt(1);\nparseInt(1, 3);\n\n0b111110111 === 503;\n0o767 === 503;\n0x1F7 === 503;\n\na[parseInt](1,2);\n\nparseInt(foo);\nparseInt(foo, 2);\n</code></pre>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/prefer-numeric-literals

prefer-spread	A			ECMAScript 6\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>Before ES2015, one must use <code>Function.prototype.apply()</code> to call variadic functions.</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var args = [1, 2, 3, 4];\nMath.max.apply(Math, args);\n</code></pre>\n<p>In ES2015, one can use the spread operator to call variadic functions.</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">/*eslint-env es6*/\n\nvar args = [1, 2, 3, 4];\nMath.max(...args);\n</code></pre>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule is aimed to flag usage of <code>Function.prototype.apply()</code> in situations where the spread operator could be used instead.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/prefer-spread

require-yield	A			ECMAScript 6\nRecommended Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(recommended) The <code>&quot;extends&quot;: &quot;eslint:recommended&quot;</code> property in a configuration file enables this rule.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule generates warnings for generator functions that do not have the <code>yield</code> keyword.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/require-yield
rest-spread-spacing	A			ECMAScript 6\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>ES2015 introduced the rest and spread operators, which expand an iterable structure into its individual parts. Some examples of their usage are as follows:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">let numArr = [1, 2, 3];\nfunction add(a, b, c) {\n    return a + b + c;\n}\nadd(...numArr); // -&gt; 6\n\nlet arr1 = [1, 2, 3];\nlet arr2 = [4, 5, 6];\narr1.push(...arr2); // -&gt; [1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]\n\nlet [a, b, ...arr] = [1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\na; // -&gt; 1\nb // -&gt; 2\narr; // -&gt;  [3, 4, 5]\n\nfunction numArgs(...args) {\n  return args.length;\n}\nnumArgs(a, b, c); // -&gt; 3\n</code></pre>\n<p>In addition to the above, there is currently a proposal to add object rest and spread properties to the spec. They can be used as follows:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">\nlet { x, y, ...z } = { x: 1, y: 2, a: 3, b: 4 };\nx; // -&gt; 1\ny; // -&gt; 2\nz; // -&gt; { a: 3, b: 4 }\n\nlet n = { x, y, ...z };\nn; // -&gt; { x: 1, y: 2, a: 3, b: 4 }\n</code></pre>\n<p>As with other operators, whitespace is allowed between the rest or spread operator and the expression it is operating on, which can lead to inconsistent spacing within a codebase.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule aims to enforce consistent spacing between rest and spread operators and their expressions. The rule also supports the currently experimental object rest and spread properties when enabled:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-json">{\n    &quot;parserOptions&quot;: {\n        &quot;ecmaVersion&quot;: 6,\n        &quot;ecmaFeatures&quot;: {\n            &quot;experimentalObjectRestSpread&quot;: true\n        }\n    }\n}\n</code></pre>\n<p>Please read the user guide's section on <a href="http://eslint.org/docs/user-guide/configuring#specifying-parser-options">configuring parser options</a> to learn more.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/rest-spread-spacing
sort-imports	A			ECMAScript 6\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>The import statement is used to import members (functions, objects or primitives) that have been exported from an external module. Using a specific member syntax:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">// single - Import single member.\nimport myMember from &quot;my-module.js&quot;;\n\n// multiple - Import multiple members.\nimport {foo, bar} from &quot;my-module.js&quot;;\n\n// all - Import all members, where myModule contains all the exported bindings.\nimport * as myModule from &quot;my-module.js&quot;;\n</code></pre>\n<p>The import statement can also import a module without exported bindings. Used when the module does not export anything, but runs it own code or changes the global context object.</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">// none - Import module without exported bindings.\nimport &quot;my-module.js&quot;\n</code></pre>\n<p>When declaring multiple imports, a sorted list of import declarations make it easier for developers to read the code and find necessary imports later. This rule is purely a matter of style.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule checks all import declarations and verifies that all imports are first sorted by the used member syntax and then alphabetically by the first member or alias name.</p>\n<p>The <code>--fix</code> option on the command line automatically fixes some problems reported by this rule: multiple members on a single line are automatically sorted (e.g. <code>import { b, a } from 'foo.js'</code> is corrected to <code>import { a, b } from 'foo.js'</code>), but multiple lines are not reordered.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/sort-imports
symbol-description	A			ECMAScript 6						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>The <code>Symbol</code> function may have optional description:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var foo = Symbol(&quot;some description&quot;);\n\nvar someString = &quot;some description&quot;;\nvar bar = Symbol(someString);\n</code></pre>\n<p>Using <code>description</code> promotes easier debugging: when a symbol is logged the description is used:</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">var foo = Symbol(&quot;some description&quot;);\n\n&gt; console.log(foo);\n// Symbol(some description)\n</code></pre>\n<p>It may facilitate identifying symbols when one is observed during debugging.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rules requires a description when creating symbols.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/symbol-description
template-curly-spacing	A			ECMAScript 6\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<p>We can embed expressions in template strings with using a pair of <code>${</code> and <code>}</code>.</p>\n<p>This rule can force usage of spacing <em>within</em> the curly brace pair according to style guides.</p>\n<pre><code class="language-js">let hello = `hello, ${people.name}!`;\n</code></pre>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule aims to maintain consistency around the spacing inside of template literals.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/template-curly-spacing
yield-star-spacing	A			ECMAScript 6\nFixable Rules						http://eslint.org/img/logo.svg	<section class="prog__container"><p>(fixable) The <code>--fix</code> option on the <a href="../user-guide/command-line-interface#fix">command line</a> can automatically fix some of the problems reported by this rule.</p>\n<h2>Rule Details</h2>\n<p>This rule enforces spacing around the <code>*</code> in <code>yield*</code> expressions.</p>\n<p>To use this rule you either need to <a href="../user-guide/configuring">use the <code>es6</code> environment</a> or\n<a href="../user-guide/configuring">set <code>ecmaVersion</code> to <code>6</code> in <code>parserOptions</code></a>.</p>\n</section>	http://eslint.org/docs/rules/yield-star-spacing
